‚ÄúTruth is the Godhead, truth is penance; one goes to heaven by truth. Falsehood is of the form of darkness; by darkness, one is taken down. Heaven, they say, is light, and hell, darkness.

‚Äò‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§É
‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§™‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§ö ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§π‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúAffectionate words pleasing to the ears of all beings must be spoken; reviling, scandal and violence in language are forbidden; insulting others, egotism and hypocrisy are condemned.

‚Äò‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§® ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§É‡••
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúOne’s beauty is lost by (the effects of) annoying oneself; such a one falls from prosperity; his life dwindles and surely his Dharma also declines. Being without sorrow bestows happiness and excellent health.

‚Äò‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§®‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä
‡§® ‡§π‡•Ä‡§®‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•Ä‡§§‡•§
‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§â‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•á‡§§
‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§¶‡•Å‡§∂‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúOne should not hit a man at his weak points; should not speak wickedly; should not receive big things from inferior persons; should not speak that cutting word which leads one to the world of sin, the word at which another would shudder.

‚Äò‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúThe secret meaning of the Vedas is truth; of truth, sel; control; of selfbondage; this is control, release from the all-comprehensive gospel.

‚Äò‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§≤‡§¶‡•à‡§µ
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡§æ ‡§®‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§™‡•á‡§§‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ
‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúThose who are always taking pleasure in sex and eating, those who steal others’ possessions, and those men who are always violent in tongue-considering these as bereft of Dharma, the gods avoid them from a distance.‚Äù

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE SANTI PARVA.
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701784766Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡••‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡••

ANUSASANA PARVA
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701784856Screenshot2023-11-28164852.png"/>

‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ü‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§≠‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡§É‡••

Bhishma continued‚Äî

‚ÄúOne obtains a long life by good conduct; those of bad conduct die early.

‚Äò‡§™‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§® ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§§‡•à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúOne must not seek others’ wives, must avoid talking ill of others, avoid hate, stiffness, pride and severity.

‚Äò‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§∂‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§•‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•Ä‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

‚ÄúAn old man, a relative, a friend, a widowed sister, a teacher, one of a good family and a learned man, ‚Äîthese, if poor, must be protected by one according to one’s ability.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúJealousy is not conducive to longevity; therefore one should avoid jealousy.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§ó‡§æ‡§ß‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡•Ç‡§¶‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•á ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúOne must bathe in the sacred waters, deep, clear and pure, of his own mind, in the lake of firmness and at the ford of Truth.

‚Äò‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡•ã ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§Æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúPenance, Knowledge, Softness, Truthfulness, Straightforwardness, Non-injury to all beings, Sympathy, Self-control, Tranquillity, ‚Äîthese constitute purity by bath in waters.

‚Äò‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∂‡•å‡§ö‡§Æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúPurity of conduct is the great purity; the purity by baths in sacred waters is only next to that.

‚Äò‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§°‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe great abstemious sages say that the avoiding of the eating of flesh is blessed, praise worthy, conducive to long life, helpful to attain heaven and is the great way to well-being.

‚Äò‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúHe who commits suicide in passion, anger or fear, goes to eternal hell because of his suicide.

‚Äò‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§
‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§¢‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúEvery day, thousands of occasions for sorrow, and hundreds of circumstances producing fear take possession of a fool, but not a wise man.

‚Äò‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§™‡•á‡••

‚ÄúThere is no absolute and invariable happiness even for Indra in his heaven.

‚Äò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§™‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúAll accumulations end in loss; all rises end in fall; all unions end in separation; and life ends in death.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á
‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúThere is trouble in earning riches; trouble in guarding the riches earned; trouble if they are lost, trouble if they are spent; fie on wealth, the store-house of miseries.

‚Äò‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§® ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§∞‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§≤‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§É‡••

‚ÄúSeeing so well those who are being born and those who are, in the same manner, dying, if a man is not violently disturbed, he is verily equal to a piece of wood or a lump of clay.

‚Äò‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThis has been described as the best means of attaining the summum bonum,‚Äî the continuous meditation of Lord Narayana, worshipping Him, making offerings to Him and singing His praises,

‚Äò‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§ó‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúSinging the praise of the Lord of the universe, the God of gods, the Infinite and Supreme Being with His thousand names, one surmounts all misery.

‚Äò‡§è‡§∑ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúThis Dharma I consider the greatest of all Dharmas, namely, that man should always worship with devotion and hymns the Lotus-eyed Lord, Narayana.

‚Äò‡§® ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß‡•ã ‡§® ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§® ‡§≤‡•ã‡§≠‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡••

‚ÄúIn the blessed who are the devotees of Lord Narayana, there is no anger, no malice, no avarice, no evil thought.

‚Äò‡§è‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§ï‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ó‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É‡••

‚ÄúThe one Vishnu, the Great Being, the Soul of all beings, the Enjoyer of the universe, the Imperishable Lord, pervades and enjoys the various separate beings and (all) the three worlds.

‚Äò‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á
‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡•Å‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡§µ‡•á‡•§
‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á
‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ã‡§ü‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ó‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡•á ‡§®‡§Æ‡§É‡••

‚ÄúObeisance unto that Imperishable Being, of thousand forms, of thousand feet, eyes, heads and hands; obeisance unto that Eternal Being of thousand names, who has in Himself thousands of crores of aeons of Time.

‚Äò‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

‚Äú(Yudhisthira,) protect all your subjects; let Krishna be your greatest refuge;‚Äù having said thus, the wise Bhishma stopped for meditating (upon the Lord).

‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§π ‡§µ‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‚Äô

When Bhishma had become silent, Vyasa hastened and said: ‚ÄúKing (Bhishma)! Yudhisthira, the Kuru king, is composed (by this discourse of yours); you must give him leave to go to his city.‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§®‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§µ‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§É‡••

King Bhishma, son of the Ganges and Santanu, gave leave to Yudhisthira and his ministers and told him sweetly:

‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ö ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ã ‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•á‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúKing, go to your City; let your mind be set on Dharma; son of Pritha (Kunti); You will attain good fortune; let your mind’s fever disappear; you must come (here again to me) when the sun has begun to go northwards from the South.‚Äù

‡§§‡§•‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§â‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡§ó‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡•§
‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§¨‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∏‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§É‡••

Saying that he would do so, Yudhisthira went to Hastinapura. After living in his excellent city for fifty nights, and seeing then that the sun had returned (from the South), king Yudhisthira, surrounded by his retinue, came to Bhishma in Kurukshetra.

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ] ‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ß ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúKing ! son of the Ganges! I am Yudhisthira; obeisance unto you; I have come in the specified time. King Dhritarashtra has come with his ministers; also the valorous Krishna.‚Äù

‚Äò‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ó‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§•‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡••

‚ÄúFortunately, you have come, Yudhisthira; the sun has changed his course (from the south towards the north).‚Äù After saying thus to Yudhisthira, the son of God Dharma, and after taking leave of Dhritarashtra, Bhishma said these words to Dhritarashtra at that time:

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡§µ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡§É
‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∂‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á ‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúKing (Dhritarashtra) ! By Dharma, these are as much your sous as of Pandu. Standing by Dharma, protect them who take pleasure in the service of the elders. Your sons were evil-natured; you must not grieve for them.‚Äù

‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§§ ‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡§É‡••

Bhishma (then) addressed Krishna of mighty arm:

‚Äò‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§π‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ï‡§≤‡•á‡§¨‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••’

‚ÄúGod, Lord of the god of gods, bowed to by gods and demons! I know you as the divine, ancient and greatest sage, Narayana. Give me leave, Krishna, I will cast off this body.‚Äù

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•§
‡§® ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•É‡§ú‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§É‡••

Krishna‚Äî

‚ÄúKing Bhishma, I give you leave; join the Vasus; there is no sin in you; you have the godhead which is of the pure spirit.‚Äù

‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§•‡•§
‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§‚Äô
‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡••

‚ÄúI desire to give up my life (now); you must all give me leave for it; you must strive for Truth; Truth is the greatest strength.‚Äù Having said so to all the Kurus, Bhishma became at that time, rid of the arrow-heads (that had pierced into his body).

‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§≠‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§π‡••

The vital breaths werecontrolled by him at all the centres, and breaking open his head, his soul shot up heavenwards.

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡§ö ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡••
‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

With showers of flowers, there arose sounds of the celestial drums; and the Siddhas and the Brahmarishis rejoiced saying ‚Äògood, good‚Äô.

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É‡••
‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ä‡§∞‡§• ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§´‡§ø‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡••

Performing the crematory rites to the body of Bhishma, the greatest of the Kauravas, all the Kauravas went to the holy Ganges and offered then the manes’ libation to Bhishma.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE ANUSASANA PARVA.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701838488Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡•• ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡••
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701838544Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

ASVAMEDHIKA PARVA
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701838544Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ã‡§¶‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§®‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡§ó‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Having offered the manes’ libation (to Bhishma), the mighty-armed Yudhisthira, with tearful eyes entered Hastinapura, after being consoled by Lord Krishna.

‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§§ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡•§
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∂‡§∞‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§É‡••

Along with his brothers, the righteous Yudhisthira ruled the world, even as the emperor Manu, even as Rama, son of

Dasaratha. There was nothing unrighteous in Yudhisthira’s kingdom; all people loved Dharma.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§∂‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡§É‚Äô‡••

Then was born Parikshit, a still-born child, as a result of the Brahma Astra of Asvatthaman. Meeting her brother, Subhadra told these words, afflicted with grief: O inviolable Krishna! I entreat you, let this son of Abhimanyu come to life.‚Äù

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§è‡§∑ ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‚Äú‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡•å‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡§É‡••
‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§∏ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Krishna‚Äî

‚ÄúEven as all beings are looking on, I will bring this (dead child) to life. ‚ÄòIf Truth and Right are firmly established in me

for all time, let this dead child born of Abhimanyu come to life.‚Äô As soon as he was touched by Krishna with these words, the dead child attained consciousness.

‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø [‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø] ‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§π‡§∞‡§£‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Some days thereafter, Yudhisthira, the Kuru king, thought of performing the Asvamedha sacrifice.

‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•å‡§™‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã‡§π ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

When Yudhisthira had performed the final ablution after the last horse-sacrifice (of his), Lord Krishna took leave, somewhat in sorrow, of Kunti, Dhritarashtra, Gandhari, Vidura, Draupadi. Vyasa, and the other sages and ministers; He patted Subhadra and Uttara with her son, left (Yudhisthira’s) palace, and mounted His chariot.

‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∂‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§®‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ß‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•å ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

On that occasion, the Kuru king, Yudhisthira, himself took hold of the reins (of the horses of Krishna’s chariot); getting into the chariot, Arjuna took a beautiful chowrie; Ehima held Krishna’s umbrella and Nakula and Sahadeva also attended upon Krishna, waving two white chowries.

‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡•á ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å‡••

When they had crossed three yojanas6, Krishna embraced the Pandavas, gave leave to all of them who had bowed to Him, and went to Dvaraka.

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ß‡§æ‡§ú‡•Ä ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡••

And the righteous Yudhisthira enshrined Krishna in his heart and lived devoted to Him, performing his duties with mind fixed on Him, worshipping Him and completely absorbed in Him.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE ASVAMEDHIKA PARVA.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701840384Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡••‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡••
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701840472Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

ASRAMAVASIKA PARVA
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701840472Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡§§‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••

Having obtained the kingdom, the highsouled Pandavas, who had killed their enemies, protected the world, with Dhritarashtra as their head.

‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡•á ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•á [‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§É]‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡•á ‡§µ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É‡••

Then, after the fifteenth year had passed, the wise king (Dhritarashtra) felt a disgust (for life in the palace); and, waiting for the proper time to retire into the forests, he then left the palace, along with Gandhari.

‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§∏‡§π ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡•§
‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡••

Vidura also was eager to go to the forests, along with the king (Dhritarashtra); so also the chief minister and charioteer, Sanjaya, the son of Gavalga And, holding Gandhari, Kunti (also) went then.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•ã ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§§‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡••

With his followers, the old king, Dhritarashtra, proceeded to Vyasa’s hermitage. Receiving initiation there, Dhritarashtra himself entered, and made his followers also enter, the life of penance in the thermitage of (a royal sage named) Satayupa.

‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•É‡§∂‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡••

When Dhritarashtra had gone to the forests, the Pandavas, distressed very much, did not perform their royal duties, did not relish anything.

‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡••

The Pandavas then went to Dhritarashtra’s hermitage. With tears, those high-souled Pandavas worshipped king Dhritarashtra, as also Gandhari and (their own) mother (Kunti), in the prescribed manner.

‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•§
‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡••

Vidura was seen at a distance; (Yudhisthira) ran up to him with effort, said ‚ÄúI am Yudhisthira,‚Äù and stood before him.

‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§¨‡§≤‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

By the strength of his Yoga, Vidura entered the body of king Yudhisthira.

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§É‡••

As a consequence of thecurse of sage Mandavya, the celebrated God Dharna became Vidura, that God Dharma, by virtue of whose, Yudhisthira, the Kuru king, was born. Therefore, Dharma is Vidura; Vidura is Yudhisthira.

‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•à‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§É‡•§
‡§®‡§ó‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§¨‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡§É‡••

Then, king Yudhisthira, with his wife, his soldiers and kinsmen, returned to the city of Hastinapura.

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ã [‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç] ‡§Ü‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡••

The divine sage Narada came to Yudhisthira.

‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§µ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•§
‡§Ö‡§• ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡§µ‡•§

‡§¶‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§ö ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡§µ‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Narada‚Äî

‚ÄúScion of Kuru ! after you had returned from your stay in the forest, there arose a wind and there was a big forest-fire. The blessed Gandhari and your mother Kunti were consumed by the forest-fire ; and so also, your uncle, the king (Dhritarashtra). The intelligent Sanjaya went away to the Himalaya mountain.‚Äù

‡§è‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡••

On hearing this, everybody grieved very much. After consoling King Yudhisthira, Narada departed.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE ASRAMAVASIKA PARVA.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701841455Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡••‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Æ‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡••
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701841517Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

MAUSALA PARVA
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701841517Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§• ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡••

When the thirty-sixth year after the battle came, Yudhisthira saw inauspicious portents.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•Ä‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§π‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§∂‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§É‡••

Observing then the change in the times that had taken place and desiring to make true what Gandhari had said (namely, that thekinsmen of Krishna killing each other), Krishna, would perish, the subduer of his enemies, ordered an excursion to a water-side.

‡§π‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡•á ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡•á ‡§§‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ú‡§ò‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∏‡§≤‡•à‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ß‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The merry Yadavas camped with their wives at Prabhasa at that time. Those Yadavas of fiery valour had a big carouse at Prabhasa. Impelled by Fate, they struck each other with pestles in a fight. Intoxicated and fighting one another, they fell.

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç
‚Äò‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§‚Äô
‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

At that time, Krishna ordered Daruka, (his charioteer): ‚ÄúInform Arjuna of the destruction of the Yadus.‚ÄùThen, he entered the city of Dvaraka and told his father (Vasudeva):

‚Äò‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•Å ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç
‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§¨‡•ã‡§ß ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á
‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúPlease, protect everything belonging to us, looking forward to Arjuna’s arrival; know it from me that I will go to the forest and perform penance, along with Balarama.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•Ä‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂
‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§®‡§æ‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§ó‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Having said this in this manner, Krishna met Balarama standing alone in a lonely forest; He then saw a serpent entering the seas from out of the mouth of that Balarama in Yoga.

‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç
‡§∂‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡§∏‡•Ä ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ
‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Krishna then thought that it was time for his passage (to His own world); (and so) he lay down, entering upon deep Yoga; pervading heaven and earth with his splendour, that Master of Yoga, the Supreme Spirit, reached His own inscrutable place.

‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§Æ‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••

And Daruka also reached the Kuru country, saw the great warriors, the Pandavas, and told them of the Vrishnis mutually destroyed in a pestle-fight.

‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É, ‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§π [‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•ã]‡••

The Pandavas were afflicted with grief (and) the dear friend of Krishna, Arjuna, went along with Daruka, to see his uncle (Vasudeva).

‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§® ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡§≤‡§æ‡§™ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•Å‡§É‡§ñ‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ö‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡••

Embracing Arjuna, the aged Vasudeva wept, being greatly distressed. And extremely sad, Arjuna said these words in the proper time:

‚Äò‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúI shall myself take all the Vrishnis and the Andhakas to Indraprastha. This Vajra (son of Aniruddha, Krishna’sgrandson) will be your king at Sakraprastha.‚Äù

‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§• ‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•å‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

On the following day then, Vasudeva attained to heaven.

‡§∏ ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É‡••

After performing in the prescribed manner the obsequial rites for the departed Vrishnis, Arjuna mounted the chariot and sped on the seventh day.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

The ladies of the (departed) Vrishni heroes followed Arjuna.

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§§‡•§
‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§≤‡§ø‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ó‡§∞‡§É‡••

As that best of men, Arjuna, left part after part of that land of the Vrishnis, the sea flooded it with its waters.

‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§≠‡§∏‡•ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡§≠‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡•á‡§® [‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§]‡••
‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡••

Then, on seeing the ladies, with their lords dead, being taken by Arjuna, himself alone, thieves became greedy and impelled by the change in Time, they fell upon (the party) for (looting) their wealth.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§∂‡•á‡§® ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡••

Arjuna made an effort to protect the people. (But), owing to the utter loss of his missiles and owing to the decrease in the power of his arm, Arjuna became dejected, thinking ‚Äúit is Fate‚Äù.

‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§É‡••

Taking with him those that survived (the attack by the robbers), Arjuna entered Kurukshetra, and with the permission of Yudhisthira, he settled at different places the princes who were to continue the Vrishni race.

‡§¨‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§Æ‡•á‡••

With eyes shrouded by tears, Arjuna met Vyasa sitting in his hermitage.

‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Å‡§®‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ò‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§ú‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§£ ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§É‡••

‡§Æ‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É‡••
‡§∂‡•ã‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ó‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§≠‡§∏‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∂‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§ö‡•§
‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§É‡••
‡§® ‡§ö‡•á‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§É‡••
‡§á‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§§‡§∞‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•É‡§£‡•Å ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§ß‡§®‡•§
‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•å ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§¶‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•à‡§É‡••
‡§ß‡§®‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡§£‡•á‡•§
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡•á‡•§
‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•§‚Äô

Arjuna‚Äî

‚ÄúThat beautiful Krishna of body like the cloud and eyes like a big lotus, has, along with Balarama,left his body and gone to heaven. There was a terrific destruction of the Vrishni heroes in a fight with pestles. The disappearance of Krishna, I consider, is as unbelievableas the dryingup of theocean,the moving of the Mandaramountain, the

falling of the skies and the cooling of fire. And, bereft of Krishna, I do not want to stay in this world. Hear of this, O sage, more painful to me than that: Sage, even as I was seeing, the Abhiras of the Panchanada region overpowered in battle and carried away by thousands the Vrishni ladies. I took the bow there but could not string it. O great sage, the prowess of my arm is not as it was before. O best of men, you must advise what is good for me.‚Äù

‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡••
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡•Å‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡•Ä‡§π ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§® ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡•Å‡§ú‡••

Vyasa‚Äî

‚ÄúThose Vrishnis were born as partial incarnations of the gods for the protection of the bounds of Dharma and they have gone along with God Krishna; you must not grieve for them.

‚ÄúDisburdening the earth (of its evil men), the large-eyed Krishna has left his body and reached his own highest place.

‚ÄúYou best of mer. you of mighty arm! You also, with Bhima as your aid and with the twins, have achieved in this world the great mission of the gods.

‚Äò‡§¨‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•§
‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•á‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•§
‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø [‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§]‡•§
‡§è‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Ç [‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠]‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúScion of Bharata ! strength, wisdom, power and understanding appear in good times and fail (one) when times change.

‚ÄúArjuna, all this which is at the root of the world has itself its root in Time. It is time for you also to go to heaven. This, I think, is supreme good for you.‚Äù

‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ü‡§ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ï‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••

Understanding these words (of Vyasa), Arjuna went to Yudhisthira and told him all about the race of the Vrishnis and the Andhakas, as it happened.

‡•• ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE MAUSALA PARVA.
