MAHAPRASTHANA PARVA
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701844189Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡§¶‡•å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ö ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§
‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§≠‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•á ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡••

On hearing thus of the big slaughter of the Vrishnis, Yudhisthira, the king of the Kurus, entrusted the whole kingdom to Yuyutsu, installed Parikshit as king in his kingdom, removed the ornaments from his body and took to bark-garments.

‡§§‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§ú‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§ø [‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™]‡•§
‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••

Even so, all (the other brothers and Draupadi) put on bark-garments; all of them were very glad to set out (for heaven).

‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•Ä ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§ó‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡••

The five brothers, Draupadi the sixth and a dog, the seventh: thus, making seven with himself, king Yudhisthira went out of Hastinapura.

‡§¶‡§π‡§∂‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•á‡§∞‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§ø‡§ñ‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

They who had entered on Yoga, came upon Meru, the greatest of mountains.

‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡••

Falling from her Yoga, Draupadi fell down on the ground.

‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§≤‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡••

Seeing her fallen, the mighty Bhima said to Yudhisthira: ‚ÄúTell me why Draupadi has fallen on the ground.‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•á‡§£ ‡§ß‡§®‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúShe had great partiality for Arjuna especially.‚Äù

‡§∏‡§π‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§≤‡•á‡•§
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‚Äò‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‚Äô‡••

The learned Sahadeva then fell on the ground. And seeing him also fallen, Bhima spoke to king Yudhisthira: ‚ÄúWhy has this son of Madri fallen on the ground?‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§®‡•à‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§ï‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡••

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúThis Sahadeva considered none as learned as himself.‚Äù

‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§®‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§É ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡••‚Äô

Bhima‚Äî

‚ÄúNakula, matchless in the world in beauty, has fallen on the ground.‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£ ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúHis view was that there was none equal to him in beauty.‚Äù

‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã, ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡••

Seeing those three fallen, Arjuna, afflicted with grief, fell down; (and) Bhima said to king Yudhisthira:

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡••‚Äô

Of what is this the effect that Arjuna has fallen on the ground?‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‘‡§è‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§π‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§® ‡§ö ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∂‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§§‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§§‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡••

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúSingle-handed, I will burn the enemies,’ so did Arjuna say; and he did not do that ; therefore, has this Arjuna, who thought himself a hero, fallen.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§• ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§™‡§æ‡§§ ‡§π‡•à‡••

Having said so, Yudhisthira started; Bhima then fell down.

‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§≠‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡••‚Äô

Bhima‚Äî

‚ÄúOh king look, I, dear to you, am fallen.‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡•á‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúYou ate enormously and you boast because of your strength.‚Äù

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å [‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∂‡§É ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡••

Having told Bhima so, the powerful Yudhisthira went, without looking at Bhima. And that dog alone followed.

‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§û‡•ç‡§∂‡§ï‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§É‡•§
‡§∞‡§•‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Then, making heaven and earth resound all over, India came in his chariot to Yudhisthira, and asked him to ascend the chariot.

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•§
‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

King of the gods! I do not desire to go to heaven without my brothers; and let the beautiful Draupadi also go (to heaven); may you permit that.‚Äù

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§® ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§É‡••‚Äô

Indra‚Äî

‚ÄúIllustrious scion of Bharata! they have (all) gone (to heaven), casting off their human bodies. You shall surely go to heaven even with this body.‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äú‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≠‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∂ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§π‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúLord of things past and coming ! this dog has ever been devoted to me; let him go (to heaven) with me; for my heart is compassionatc.‚Äù

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‡§Ö‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç
‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••’

Indra‚Äî

‚ÄúKing, you have attained now immortality, equality with me, complete fortune, the great fulfilment of emancipation, and heaven’s happiness; abandon the dog; there is nothing cruel in it.‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúLet me not be united with that fortune, for the sake of which, I should abandon a devoted being.‚Äù

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç
‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§∏‡•á ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§®‡•Å‡••

Indra‚Äî

‚ÄúHaving abandoned your brothers and even your beloved Draupadi, how is it you do not abandon this dog also?‚Äù

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§® ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É
‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§® ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúI could not bring them to life; hence I abandoned them! I did not abandon them alive.‚Äù

‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§ö‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•Ä ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡••

On hearing those words of Yudhisthira, God Dharma spoke:

‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∂‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å [‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§]‡••

‚ÄúKing of kings! You are a worthy son of your father (Dharma), by your conduct, wisdom and this kindness towards all beings.

‚Äò‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø‡••
‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§® ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•Å‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§É‡••

‚ÄúMy son, you were tested by me before in the Dvaita forest and, desiring to secure equality between your mother and step-mother, you wished there that Nakula might come to life. (Now), you

have renounced the celestial chariot, because this dog is devoted (to you). Hence, there is no king equal to you in heaven.

‚Äò‡§Ö‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á‡§£ [‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§]‡•§
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø [‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§†] ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúTherefore, imperishable worlds shall be yours, with this (same) body; you have attained to the highest divine state.‚Äù

‡§∏‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§•‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§É‡•§
‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ω‡§Ω‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡•ã‡§¶‡§∏‡•Ä‡••

Ascending that chariot of Indra, king Yudhisthira, the most eminent of the Kuru dynasty, went up quickly pervading heaven and earth with his splendour.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE MAHAPRASTHANA PARVA.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701847308Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡•• ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§£‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡••
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701847484Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

SVARGAROHANA PARVA
<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701847484Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§™‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§π‡•§
‚Äò‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§® ‡§ï‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç‡••
‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•å ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•å ‡§ò‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡••
‡§® ‡§ö‡•á‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§µ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡••‚Äô

Reaching heaven, the righteous king Yudhisthira said: ‚ÄúThose heroic and high-souled brothers of mine of great vows, what are the worlds that are theirs now? I desire to see them; also the great Karna, son of Kunti and one who kept his promise, whom I did not know and caused

to be killed by the ambidexterous Arjuna. And I do not desire to stay here; I tell you in truth, my heaven is there where they are; I do not regard this as heaven.‚Äù‘‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§æ

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§‚Äô
‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø [‡§™‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™]‡••

‚ÄúIf you have a strong desire for thatplace where your brothersare, go there;let there be no delay.‚Äù So saying to Yudhisthira, the gods then commissioned a divine messenger to show Yudhisthira his friends.

‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡••

Then king Yudhisthira and the messenger of the gods walked the inauspicious and impassable path (of hell), taken by the sinful.

‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡•å‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

And Yudhisthira witnessed (there) the tortures of the sinful.

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúHow much of this way have we thus got to go?‚Äù

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‚Äò‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡§µ‚Äô‡••

The messenger of the gods replied tohim: ‚ÄúThus far is your progress.‚Äù

‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É‡•§
‚Äú‡§≠‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§† ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ø ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§¨‡§æ‡§ß‡§§‡•á‡••‚Äô

Returning, Yudhisthira heard words of distress from all sides: ‚ÄúOh royal saint! son of Dharma! stop for a while; when you, scion of Kuru, stand (before us), the torture does not afflict us.‚Äù

‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã ‡§ï‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§á ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•å ‡§∏‡§ö ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‚Äò‡§ï‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§•‚Äô‡••

‚ÄúAlas ! What torture !‚Äù said Yudhisthira and stopped. He said (then): ‚Äú Who are you? Why are you here?‚Äù

‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§∂‡•Å‡§É‡••

‚ÄúI am Karna.‚Äù ‚ÄúI am Bhima.‚Äù So did they cry.

‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•á‡••‚Äô

Yudhisthira‚Äî

‚ÄúWhat is that impure act done by these high-souled persons that they are in this stinking and very frightful place ?‚Äù

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ã‡§ï‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§π‡••

Yudhisthira denounced the gods and also Dharma. Burning with poignant grief, he addressed the messenger of the gods:

‚Äò‡§® ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•á‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúInform (the gods) that I am not going there (to heaven); I am staying (here, in hell); for, by my association, these brothers of mine who are afflicted become happy.‚Äù

‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§π‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§ ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã [‡§®‡•É‡§™]‡•§
‡§® ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•å‡••

When Yudhisthira stayed (there) for a while, that darkness (of hell) disappeared; tortures were not seen; and a pure breeze then blew.

‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•å‡§ï‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡§ó‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡•§

The denizens of heaven came to where king Yudhisthira was.

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî

‡§® ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•Å ‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§£ ‡§â‡§™‡§ö‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡••

Indra‚Äî

‚Äú(Yudhisthira !) You must not become angry; hear these words of mine: Hell must be seen by all kings without fail; it is under cover of some pretext that you deceived Drona in respect of his son; hence has hell been shown to you: through some pretext.

‚Äò‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á ‡•§
‡§è‡§∑‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§®‡§¶‡•Ä ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡•§
‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‚Äô

‚ÄúAll of them have gone to heaven, those for whom you grieve. Yudhisthira, here is the holy Ganges, the celestial river, the purifier of the three worlds. By your bathing here, your mortal nature will disappear.‚Äù

‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É‚Äî

‚Äò‡§≠‡•ã ‡§≠‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§§‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•§
‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§É‡•§
‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø‡••
‡§® ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§®‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç‡§™‡§§‡•á‡•§
‡§™‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§π‡§ø ‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§† ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡••‚Äô

Dharma‚Äî

‚ÄúOh, most wise king! my son! I am pleased with you. Previously, you were tested by me with questions in the Dvaita forest; again, I tested you there (in your journey to heaven), taking the form of a

dog; and this is the third test, (which you have stood) by your desiring to stand for the good of your brothers. Son of Kunti! king! your brothers do not deserve hell; come, come, you best of the Bharatas! meet them who have gone to heaven.‚Äù

‡§ó‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§®‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ó‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Bathing then in the sacred and sanctifying celestial river, the Ganges that is lauded by the sages, king Yudhisthira cast off his mortal frame.

‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•à‡§É‡•§
‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ó‡•ã‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§´‡§≤‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§æ‡•§
‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§≠‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§∏‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§®‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§™‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§≤‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

Becoming then divine-bodied and along with gods and sages, Yudhisthira saw- there Krishna, along with the lustrous.

Arjuna ; he saw theninanother place Karna, the best ofwarriors;then Bhimasena, endowed witha divine form, Nakula and Sahadeva and similarly Draupadi, garlanded with lotuses and lilies.

‡§µ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§• ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§£‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§ß‡§®‡•á‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡•§
‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•å‡•§
‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§É [‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠]‡•§
‡§ß‡•É‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡•§
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏ ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§®‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡§π‡••

Bhishma of great lustre became one of the Vasus themselves. Drona became one with Brihaspati, the foremost of the sons of Angiras. Dhritarashtra attained the unobtainable worlds of Kubera Accompanied by his two wives, Pandu went to the great Indira’s abode Karna who was killed (in the battle) entered the Sun.

All the sons of Dhritarashtra joined the demons. Vidura entered god Dharma, and so also king Yudhisthira.

And Krishna who was an incarnation of that eternal God of gods known as Narayana, entered (that Narayana ) at the end of His mission (on earth).

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701850154Screenshot2023-09-04170857.png"/>

‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö [‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§]‡•§
‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡§æ [‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞] ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡•§
‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§°‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§£‡§É‡••

This is the story of the Kauravas and the Pandavas, composed by the sage Vyasa, the expounder of Truth, who spread in this world the glory of the high-souled Pandavas and the sports of the Sarnga-bowed Vasudeva, the God of gods.

‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡••

One gets rid of all sins by reciting the Mahabharata.

‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§ö ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§ö [‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠]‡•§
‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡••

On Dharma, Artha, Kama and Moksha, what is found in this epic may be found elsewhere, what is not here can be seen nowhere.

‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡•§
‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ‡••

Where this great Bharata named Jaya is read, there Prosperity, Fame and Learning are present always with happiness.

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§£‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE SVARGAROHANA PARVA.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701850423Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

‡••‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

THUS ENDS THE MAHABHARATA.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701850423Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

THE MESSAGE OF THE MAHABHARATA
BY DR. V. RAGHAVAN, M.A., Ph.D.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701850804Screenshot2023-07-21172948.png"/>

THE Mahabharata of Sage Vyasa is comparable only to the Ramayana of sage Valmiki in its hold over the millions of Hindus, a hold which the Titan of Time has failed to render less strong. Dharmaputra is still the inspiring example of all who have made truthfulness and righteousness the only motive force of their action; Karna is still the greatest object of comparison for the munificent; Arjuna, the Nara, is still loved as the ideal man. And which Hindu is there, whom the faith does not sustain that in his hour of trial, when everybody has forsaken him, the Lord who saved Draupadi will come to his rescue?

While the Ramayana is cherished as the first among the Kavyas, the Mahabharata is revered as the fifth Veda, and its author, the Rishi Krishna Dvaipayana Vyasa, is looked upon as no other than God Narayana himself; for, the verse adds, who else can be the author of the great Bharata? The Epic is great in every sense. Besides being the epic poem narrating the story of the house of the Kurus, it is, so to say, the cultural encyclop√¶dia of the Hindus. The

The Epic says of itself: ‚ÄúOn Dharma, Artha, Kama and Moksha, what is found here is found elsewhere, what is not present here can be seen nowhere else.‚Äù

Nothing less than Truth and Right, Satya and Dharma, form the theme of the great Epic. Sanskrit literary critics have stated that Poetry has its immediate purpose in the readers’ enjoyment of its art and its next purpose in the moral awakening which takes place in the readers’ hearts. The latter, the Dharma Vyutpatti, is an Injunction calling us to do as Rama and Yudhisthira did and to shun what Ravana and Duryodhana did. This Injunction is dissolved in the medium of poetry and is not apparent at first sight; it is not expressed, but being unmistakably implied in it, suggests itself to the reader. In effect, the poet’s subtle Injunction and Prohibition are more powerful than those shouted from the pulpit. The Mahabharata describes itself as a poem, Kavya, in the beginning (1.1-97) and it is as Kavya that Anandavardhana, the greatest of Sanskrit literary critics, studies the Mahabharata towards the end of his classic, the Dhvanyaloka. He has brilliantly expounded there the final purport of the Great Epic as the realisation of the vanity of earthly glories and as the attainment of Dharma, Vairagya, Santi and Moksha. The changes in values brought about by the passage of Time prove the vanity of all earthly glories (Santi Parva,

Moksha Dharma, 178,4) and hence it is that both at the beginning and the end, the Epic has glorified (1. 1. 272-275 and XVI. 9. 36-40). This Vairagya, together with Dharma, forms the means of our realising God and attaining Liberation. Anandavardhana observes:

When Vyasa says that in his Epic, he has sung of the Lord and when he describes his epic as the Story of Narayana‚Äù Narayana Katha his message is:‚ÄúThe history of the Pandavas is only the argument; the case is the greatness of the Lord. Revel in love for Him and wallow not in the worthless things of the world.‚Äù (Dhvanyaloka, pp. 238-9). When one understands this, the huge Epic atonce attains a unity of character. The Pandavas represent Dharma, which alone is the path to God; Duryodhana, his brothers and his allies represent Adharma. The story of the Epic is the conflict of the two. The Lord Himself, Bhishma, Vidura and Drona try their best to save Duryodhana by pointing out to him the superiority of Dharma; but doomed by Fate, the unthinking prince ruins himself and his allies. This Dharma is the message of the Great Epic and it can hardly be missed. As the Epic opens, it says: (I.1.76) ‚ÄúVyasa sang of the greatness of Lord Vasudeva and the truthfulness of the Pandavas.‚Äù And as the Epic closes, it says: (XVIII. 5. 76-7)

‚ÄúWith uplifted hands, I shout; alas! none

heeds. From Dharma can one attain his Artha and Kama. Why is not that Dharma resorted to? Not out of passion, not out of fear, not out of avarice, not even for the sake of life, should one abandon Dharma. This is the essence; this is the Bharata Gayatri. Meditate upon this as you rise out of bed every morning.‚Äù

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701853078Screenshot2023-07-21172948.png"/>

INDEX TO THE PROPER NAMES
OCCURRING IN THE TEXT

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1701853150Screenshot2023-06-15124029.png"/>

** ABHIMANYU‚Äî** Son of Arjunaand Subhadra; marries Uttara, daughter of king Virata; meets with a cruel death in the great war; father of Parikshit. Also called Arjuni (son of Arjuna), Karshni (son of Krishna,a name of Arjuna), Saubhadra and Saubhadreya (son of Subhadra).

**ADHIRATHA‚Äî**Of the Suta caste of charioteers and bards; rescues Karna from the waters and brings him up as his own son; thus Karna’s foster-father.

ADITYAS‚Äî The gods, the Devas or the twelve Devas of that name.

AGNI.‚Äî God of fire; burns the Khandava forest with the help of Arjuna and Krishna. Other names, Pavaka, Havyavaha.

** AMARAVATI.‚Äî**The capital of Indra in heaven.

** AMBA.‚Äî** The eldest daughter of the Kasi king; brought by force by Bhishma to be given in marriage to Vichitravirya; desires to be set free to marry Salva.

** AMBALIKA.‚Äî** Third daughter of the Kasi king; the second wife of Vichitravirya; through Vyasa’s Niyoga, bears Pandu.

** AMBIKA.‚Äî** Second daughter of the Kasi king; first wife of Vichitravirya; through Vyasa’s Niyoga, bears the blind Dhritarashtra.

**ANDHAKAS‚Äî**A clan of people, kinsmen of Krishna.

ANGAS.‚Äî A territory in the east; of which Duryodhana, with the consent of his father and Bhishma, makes Karna the king.

** ANGIRAS.‚Äî** A Brahmarshi, father of Brihaspati.

**ANTAKA.‚Äî**The god of death; has a noose in the hand hence described as Pasahasta; the same as god Dharma, father of Yudhisthira.

ARJUNA.‚Äî Third Pandava; born of Kunti when she invoked Indra, hence known as Indratmaja.

Other names: Partha, Kaunteya, etc., (son of Pritha or Kunti), Phalguna (born in the constellation of Uttaraphalguni), Madhyama Pandava (the middle-born of the five brothers), Bibhatsu (because he never did anything loathsome), Kiriti, Kiritamali, (because he always wore on his head a golden diadem given to him by Indra), Pakasasani (son of Pakasasana, Indra), Jishnu (the victorious), Nara (because he was the incarnation of the ancient sage Nara, the brother of the other ancient sage Narayana, the Lord, who incarnated as Krishna), Dhananjaya (the winner of wealth), Savyasachi (ambidexterous), Gandivadhanvan

(the Gandiva-bowed), Kapidhvaja, Vanaradhvaja (having a monkey on his banner), Svetavahana (having white horses in his chariot). Also called Krishna, perhaps because of his partial identity with Krishna; hence is his son Abhimanyu called Karshni.

ASTRA.‚Äî A divine missile.

** ASVASENA.‚Äî** A serpent of the Khandava forest, which was not burnt in the forest fire.

** ASVATTHAMAN.‚Äî**Son & of Drona, Brahmacharin, a great warrior; had a jewel on his head; one of the three who survived on the side of Duryodhana in the great battle; murdered Dhrishtadyumna and the sons of the Pandavas at night and was disgraced for it by being deprived of the jewel on his head. Also referred to as Guruputra (son of the teacher), Dronaputra, Drauni, (son of Drona), Bharadvaja (grandson of Bharadvaja).

ASVATTHAMAN.‚Äî The name of an elephant ; its name is exploited to kill Drona.

ASVINS.‚Äî The twin-doctors of the Devas; celebrated for their beauty; are invoked by Madri, and give birth to the twin Pandavas, Nakula and Sahadeva.

** BAHLIKA.‚Äî**Elder brother of Santanu; oldest of the characters in the story; an elder in the Kuru court, mentioned while Krishna visits it for negotiating peace.

BAKA.‚Äî A demon living in the vicinity of the town of Ekachakra. Bhima rids the town of this demon.

** BALARAMA.‚Äî** Elder brother of Krishna; other names: Sankarshana and Rama; an incarnation of the great serpent Adisesha, on which Vishnu is lying; disappears from the world in the form of a huge serpent which issues out of his body and enters the ocean.

BHARATA.‚Äî Son of Dushyanta and Sakuntala, from whom his race takes its name; and through the race, the Epic, Mahabharata; his descendants are referred to as Bharatas; thus Dhritarashtra, Pandu, their sons and Janamejaya, the great-grandson of the Pandavas, are referred to as Bharata.

BHASKARA.‚Äî The Sun; he begets Karna on Kunti while she was a maiden.

BHIMA.‚Äî Second son of Pandu; borne by Kunti by invoking God Vayu; terrible in strength, hence Bhima; also Bhimasena; because of his great appetite, called Vrikodara; Vayuputra, Pavanatmaja, Pavani etc., (son of the Wind-god).

** BHISHMA.‚Äî** Son of Santanu and Ganga; originallycalled Devavrata; afterwardscalled Bhishma on taking the terrible vowof celibacy;the grand-old-man of the Epic; grandfather of the heroes of the story; plays a very large part in the story. Other names: Gangeya, Jahnavisuta, etc., (son of Ganga); Apagasuta, Nadisuta (son of the river, the Ganges); Santanava (son of Santanu); Pitamaha (grandfather).

Being of royal birth, he is occasionally referred to as king also, (Raja, Narendra, etc.), though he renounced the kingdom in favour of Satyavati’s sons.

BHOJAS.‚Äî A clan of people, who were kinsmen of Krishna. Kamsa, Krishna’s uncle, whom Krishna killed, was their king for some time. Krishna restored his father Ugrasena to the throne.

**BHUMINJAYA.‚Äî**The son of the Virata king; also called Vairati, Uttara and Virataputra.

BRAHMA ASTRA.‚Äî A very powerful divine missile, presided over by Brahma.

**BRIHADBALA.‚Äî**The Kosala king fighting for Duryodhana; killed by Abhimanyu.

**BRIHANNALA.‚Äî**The name assumed by Arjuna, as the eunuch teacher of dance and music at Virata’s court.

BRIHASPATI.‚Äî The preceptor of the Devas, of whom Drona was a partial incarnation; the greatest of the seven sons of the sage Angiras; Drona is absorbed into him in the end.

**CHITRANGADA.‚Äî**First son of Santanu and Satyavati; succeeded Santanu but soon died in an encounter with a Gandharva of his own name.

**CHITRASENA.‚Äî**The king of the Gandharvas who takes Duryodhana captive.

**DAMAGRANTHIN.‚Äî**Nakula’s name during his incognito life as the keeper of Virata’s horses.

**DARUKA.‚Äî**Krishna’s charioteer; carries to the Pandavas the news of the tragic end of the Yadavas.

** DASARAJA.‚Äî** Chief of the fishermen around the Jumna; foster-father of Satyavati; gives. Satyavati as wife to king Santanu, after securing for her issue promise of succession to the throne. Referred to also as Dasa (fisherman) and Ucchaissravas which seems to be his real name.

**DASARHAS.‚Äî**A clan of people who were Krishna’s kinsmen.

**DASYUS.‚Äî**A marauding tribe infesting the Panchanada region (the land the five rivers); fall upon Arjuna’s party consisting of Yadava women, and plunder the wealth and the women in the party; called also Abhiras.

**DAUSSASANI.‚Äî**Dussasana’s son; figures. among the many who jointly kill Abhimanyu; he fights Abhimanyu with his mace and strikes him dead before he could rise.

DEVADATTA.‚Äî Arjuna’s conch.

DEVAKA.‚Äî A Kshatriya of the Saurasenas; brother of Ugrasena, father of Kamsa; father of Devaki, wife of Vasudeva and mother of Krishna; thus Krishna’s maternal grandfather; had by a Sudra wife a daughter whom Vidura married; thus Krishna was Vidura’s wife’s half-sister’s son.

DEVAKI.‚Äî Krishna’s mother; wife of Vasudeva and daughter of Devaka; a half sister of hers was married to Vidura.

**DEVENDRA.‚Äî**Indra, king of the heavenly region and the Devas; is invoked by Kunti and gives birth to Arjuna, the third Pandava; also referred to by the names, Sakra, Vasava,

Mahendra, Indra, Suresvara, Devesa, Devaraja.

DHANAPATI.‚Äî Kubera; the king of the semi-divine beings, the Yakshas; lord of the northern quarter; called also Dhanesa. At the end, Dhritarashtra attains to his world.

DHATA.‚Äî The creator, God Brahma, Prajapati.

**DHARMA.‚Äî**God Dharmaraja; partially incarnated as Vidura; begot Dharmaputra alias Yudhishthira on Kunti; appears as the Yaksha in the form of a crane and tests Yudhishthira’s stand by Truth and Dharma during his forest life; and again tests Yudhishthira as a do in the great journey to heaven: Vidura and Yudhishthira are absorbed into him at the end.

**DHARTARASHTRAS.‚Äî**The hundred sons of Dhritarashtra; the anti-heroes of the Epic; the name Kauravas often applied only to them; after they are killed in the battle, it is said, they become one with the demons.

Occasionally mean also those who fought on Duryodhana’s side. The name Dhartarashtra refers to Duryodhana often.

DHAUMYA.‚Äî A Brahmana; the priest of the Pandavas.

**DHRISHTADYUMNA.‚Äî**Son of king Drupada;brother-in-law of the Pandavas; appointed commander of the Pandava forces; also called Parshata (grandson of Prishata).

**DHRITARASHTRA.‚Äî**Born of Ambika, the first wife of Vichitravirya, after his death,

through Vyasa’s Niyoga ; blind, hence referred to as Prajnachakshus (one to whom the mind alone is the eye); marries Gandhari and begets a hundred sons, Duryodhana, Dussasana, Vikarna and others; has a Vaisya wife also, who bears to him the son Yuyutsu. Called also Ambikasuta, Ambikeya (son of Ambika) and Maharajan, Rajan (king).

DRAUPADEYA.‚Äî Any one of the five sons of Draupadi; all of them are murdered by Asvatthaman in a nocturnal attack on the sleeping camp of the Pandava forces.

DRAUPADI.‚Äî The queen of the Pandavas; daughter of king Drupada (hence Draupadi); her name is Krishna; also called Panchali, because she is the daughter of the Panchala king; Parshati, since she was the grand-daughter of Prishata; and Yajnaseni, daughter of Yajnasena, which is another name of Drupada.

DRONA.‚Äî A Brahmin; master of the Dhanurveda, themilitary science; the preceptor of the sons of Dhritarashtra and Pandu, of Karna, and of Dhrishtadyumna; hence referred to simply as Acharya. He was a partial incarnation of Brihaspati, the preceptor of the Devas. Also referred to as Bharadvaja (son of Bharadvaja).

**DRUPADA.‚Äî**King of the Panchalas; belongs to the Somaka line; father of Sikhandi, Dhrishtadyumna and Draupadi; father-in-law of the five Pandavas. Other names: Parshata (son of Prishata), Yajnasena, Panchalya, Saumaki (grandson of Somaka).

** DURYODHANA.‚Äî** Eldest son of Dhritarashtra and Gandhari; the anti-hero of the Epic. Also called Suyodhana, Dhartarashtra, etc., (son of Dhritarashtra), Gandhari (son Gandhari), Raja, Nripa, Kururaja etc., because he was king.

DUSSALA.‚Äî The one daughter of Dhritarashtra and Gandhari; given in marriage to Jayadratha, the king of the Sindhus.

**DUSSASANA.‚Äî**Duryodhana’s brother andassociateinevil deeds; second son of Dhritarashtra; also referred to as Rajavaraja, brother of the king (i.e., Duryodhana).

** DVAITAVANA.‚Äî**A part of the Kamyaka forest; also the name of a sacred lake in the Kamyaka forest. The exiled Pandavas spend part of their forest-life on its banks.

**DVARAKA.‚Äî**Krishna’s island-city in the sea in the west; submerged in the waters after He left the world.

**EKACHAKRA.‚Äî**The town which the Pandavas first reach after their escape from the lac house; the brothers live there disguised as Brahmins for some time; and during this time, Bhima kills the demon Baka who was infesting that town.

GADA.‚Äî Ahalf-brother of Krishna; describes Arjuna’s qualities to his sister Subhadra and Subhadra’s qualities to Arjuna. As elder brother of this Gada, Krishna is called Gadagraja.

**GANDHAMADANA.‚Äî**A part of the Himalayas; lies between Siva’s Kailasa and Kubera’s Alaka.

** GANDHARI.‚Äî** Daughter of the king of the Gandharas, Subala, hence called Subalatmaja; wife of Dhritarashtra and mother of Duryodhana and others.

**GANDHARVAS.‚Äî**A class of divine beings; they assail Duryodhana’s forces and take captive Duryodhana and others, while the latter are on a trip to their cattle-farms in the Kamyaka forest.

GANDIVA.‚Äî Name of Arjuna’s bow.

GANGA.‚Äî The divine Ganges; marries Santanu; gives birth to eight sons; throws seven into the waters, sparing the eighth, (Bhishma), and leaves Santanu.

**GHATOTKACHA.‚Äî**Demon-son of Bhima and Hidimba; appears in the great battle on the side of the Pandavas with an army of demons and after doing havoc during a nocturnal fight, is killed by Karna with his Sakti missile.

GOPAS.‚Äî Shepherd forces of Krishna; also called Narayanas.

HARI.‚Äî The Supreme Lord who is also the Krishna of this epic. Other names of His occurring in this text are Hrishikesa, Vishnu, etc. See under Krishna.

HASTINAPURA.‚Äî The capital of the Bharatas; other names: Hastinaman, Nagasahvaya, Gajasahvaya, Nagapura.

HIDIMBA.‚Äî A demon whom Bhima kills in the forest adjacent to Varanavata.

HIDIMBA.‚Äî The sister of the above mentioned demon, Hidimba; loves Bhima; permitted by Kunti to have Bhima as

husband; bears to Bhima the son named Ghatotkacha.

HIMAVAN.‚Äî The Himalayas; the Pandavas spend part of their exile-life on its slopes; Arjuna performs his penance on one of its summits.

HRADA.‚ÄîThe lake named Dvaipayana in the battle-field of Kurukshetra, where Duryodhana hides himself, after his armies are completely destroyed.

INDRADHVAJA.‚ÄîIndra’s banner, worshipped in ancient days.

**INDRAPRASTHA.‚Äî**Yudhisthira’scapital; old name, Khandavaprastha.

ISHIKA ASTRA.‚Äî A dreadful missile charged with incantation; Asvatthaman lets it on Uttara’s womb, so that the Pandava line may become extinct.

JAYA.‚ÄîA name of the Epic, the Mahabharata.

JAYADRATHA.‚ÄîKing of the Sindhus; son-in-law of Dhritarashtra, brother-in-law of Duryodhana, and husband of Dussala; plays a prominent part in killing Abhimanyu, Arjuna’s son, in the great battle and is killed by Arjuna. Also called Saindhavaka, Saindhava, Sindhuraja.

KAMYAKA.‚Äî A forest where the Pandavas spend a large part of their exile-life; it was near the river Sarasvati. The Dvaita forest also forms part of it.

KANKA.‚Äî Meansa falseBrahmin;Yudhisthira assumesit as his name

when he lives as & Brahmin courtier of king Virata.

KAPI.‚Äî A monkey; the ensign on the banner of Arjuna’s chariot presented to him by Agni. Later, for Bhima’s sake, his half-brother, Anjaneya-Hanuman, infuses himself into the form of this monkey on Arjuna’s banner, during the great battle.

KARNA.‚Äî First-born son of Kunti; born (while she was a maiden in her foster-father’s house) on her invoking God Sun, and hence called Vaikartana, Adityanandana (born of the Sun) and so on; left by Kunti on the waters of the river; brought up by a charioteer named Adhiratha, (hence called Adhirathi, Sutaputra, etc.) and his wife Radha, (hence called Radheya); the main strength of Duryodhana; great archer; celebrated for his munificence. Also
called Vrisha.

**KARTAVIRYA.‚Äî**An ancient Haihaya king who ruled on the banks of the Narmada; a very great warrior; had a thousand hands; also known as Arjuna and Kartavirya Arjuna; mentioned here as an object of comparison for valour and strength.

**KASIPATI.‚Äî**King of the Kasis; offers three daughters in Svayamvara to the kings; the first wants to marry the king of the Saubhas; the other two marry Vichitravirya, Santanu’s second son.

KAUNTEYA.‚Äî Son of Kunti.**‚Äî**Yudhisthira, or Bhima or. Arjuna.

** KAURAVA.‚Äî** Any scion of the Kuru house, Dhritarashtra, Pandu, or any son of either.

KHANDAVA.‚Äî Name of the forest on the bank of the Jumna and adjacent to Yudhisthira’s capital, (Indraprastha) Kandavaprastha.

KHANDAVAPRASTHA.‚Äî The city which Yudhishthira was given to rule over by Dhritarashtra; it was renamed Indraprastha after being rebuilt and made Yudhisthira’s capital.

**KICHAKA.‚Äî**The brother-in-law of king Virata and his commander-in-chief; makes
advances to Draupadi and is killed by Bhima.

KRIPA.‚Äî A Brahmana; first preceptor of the sons of Dhritarashtra and Pandu; brother-in-law of Drona who took his place; son of Saradvan, hence called Saradvata; brother of Saradvati, wife of Drona; one of the three survivors on Duryodhana’s side, in the great battle. Also referred to as Gautama, a Gotra name.

**KRISHNA.‚Äî**An incarnation of God Narayana; the dominating personality of the Bharata; of the race of the Yadavas and the Vrishnis and hence called Yadava and Varshneya; the strengthof the Pandavas,who are his aunt Kunti’ssons; also referred to by the following names: Kamsa Kaliya Sudana (the destroyer of his tyrant-uncle Kamsa and the serpent Kaliya), Kamalapatraksha and Pundarikaksha (of lotus eyes), Isvara, Sarvesvara (Lord, Lord of all), Hari, Kesava, Vasudeva,

Jagannatha, Madhava, Satvata (of the Satvata race), Achyuta, Dasarha (of the Dasarha race), Bhutaguru (Lord of all beings), Gopa (because he lived in childhood among the cowherds of Brindavan), Janardana, Chakragadapani (one who has the discus and mace in his hands), Kesihan (the destroyer of the demonKesin), Pushkarekshana(becausehe had eyes like full-blown lotuses), Dvarakanilaya or D.‚Äîvasin (denizen of Dvaraka), Govinda, Yadavanandana (a scion of the Yadava line), Mahayogin (the Great Mystic), Visvatman (Soul of the Universe), Visvabhavana (Creator of the Universe), Tribhuvanesvara (Lord of the three worlds), Hrishikesa, Madhusudana (destroyer of the demon Madhu), Devakiputra (son of Devaki), Sauri (grandson of Sura), Purushottama, Lokanatha, Gadagraja (elder brother of Gada), Andhakavrishninatha, Yadupravira, Vrishnisimha, Vrishnikulapravira, Yadukulodvaha, Vishtarasravas, Vishnu, Bhagavan,Devadevesa,Purana Rishi, Yogacharya,Sarngadhanvan, Sarngin (armed with the Sarnga bow).

** KRITAVARMAN.‚Äî** The only Yadava chief who fights in the great war for Duryodhana; son of Hridika, hence called Hardikya; one of the three survivors on Duryodhana’s side; Satvata (because he belonged to that race).

**KURU.‚Äî**An ancestor of the Bharatas; the race is named after him also; thus the

heroes of the Epic are called Kurus, Kauravas, Kauravyas, Kurunandanas and Kurusattamas.

KURUKSHETRA.‚Äî The great battle-field; the place where the Gandharva named Chitrangada and Chitrangada, Santanu’s first son by Satyavati, fight and the latter is killed; the place where the great battle of the Epic takes place for eighteen days.

MADANA.‚Äî Cupid, god of Love.

MADRESVARA.‚Äî King of the Madras; father of Madri, mother of the last two Pandavas, Nakula and Sahadeva, the twins; father of Salya, the uncle of the Pandavas.

MADREYA.‚Äî A son of Madri, Nakula or Sahadeva.

MADRI.‚Äî Daughter of the king of the Madras; sister of Salya; second wife of Pandu; invokes the Asvins and begets the twins, Nakula and Sahadeva, the last two Pandavas; mounts her husband’s funeral pyre, leaving her sons to Kunti’s care. Referred otherwise also as Madrarajasuta and Madravati.

**MANDAVYA.‚Äî**A sage named Mandavya or Animandavya cursed GodYamadharma as a consequence of which Yamadharma partially incarnated himself as Vidura.

MANU.‚Äî The first and greatest of the kings of ancient India; son of Visvasvan (Sun); founder of the solar race; greatest exemplar of righteous rule.

**MATSYAS.‚Äî**The name of Virata’s country.

**MARUTS.‚Äî**The gods, the Devas.

**MAYA.‚Äî**The architect of the demons; he was in the Khandava forest while it was being burnt by Agni with the help of Krishna and Arjuna. In return for saving him, Maya builds for the Pandavas an excellent hall in their capital.

MERU.‚Äî A mythological golden mountain, biggest of all mountains, the centre around which the Sun and the Moon revolve.

NAGA ASTRA.‚Äî Serpent-missile which Karna aims at Arjuna and from which Krishna contrives to save Arjuna by sinking the chariot.

NAKULA.‚Äî Fourth Pandava, son of Madri; noted for his beauty. Also referred to as Madreya, (son of Madri).

NARA.‚Äî An ancient sage, brother of sage Narayana, who is none else than God Narayana. Nara incarnates as Arjuna; he is partially identical with Narayana.

NARADA.‚Äî One of the chief celestial sages; son of Brahma.

**NARA-NARAYANA-ASRAMA.‚Äî**The penancegrove of Nara and Narayana in the Himalayas. NARAYANA. The ancient sage of that name who is God Himself.

**OGHAVATI.‚Äî**A stream on the banks of which the Pandavas and Krishna stay for the night, after the battle comes to an end on the eighteenth day; and on whose banks Bhishma lies on a bed of arrows till Uttarayana.

**PANCHAJANYA.‚Äî**Krishna’s conch.

** PANCHALAS.‚Äî** The country ruled by king Drupada; gives the naine Panchala to Drupada and Panchali to Draupadi.

**PANCHANADA.‚Äî**The region of the five rivers; the Punjab.

PANDAVAS.‚Äî The five sons of Pandu; the heroes of the Epic; also referred to by the general names Bharatas. Kauravas, Kauravyas, Kurunandanas, Panduputras etc.

**PANDAVEYA.‚Äî**Son of Pandu; another form of the word ‚ÄòPandava‚Äô.

PANDU.‚Äî Born of Ambalika, second wife of Vichitravirya through Vyasa’s Niyoga; marries Kunti and Madri; father of the five Pandavas, the heroes of the Epie. Also referred to as Ambalikasuta (son of Ambalika).

**PARIKSHIT.‚Äî**Son of Abhimanyu and Uttara; born a corpse as a result of the deadly missile aimed at his mother’s womb by Asvatthaman; Krishna brings him to life by his power; succeeds the Pandavas on the throne; father of Janamejaya, to whom Vaisampayana, at the bidding of Vyasa, narrates the Mahabharata.

PARTHA.‚Äî A son of Pritha orKunti: Yudhisthira or Bhima or Arjuna refers mainly to Arjuna; cf. Parthasarathi, a name of Krishna.

PRABHASA.‚Äî A Tirtha in West India; a waterside to which the Yadava tribes go for making merry and where they destroy themselves by mutual fight.

PRACHYAS.‚Äî The people of the east.

PRAMANAKOTI.‚Äî A wooden structure used as bathing stand, projecting into the Ganges; Bhima, who was sleeping there, tired after swimming, was thrown into the Ganges by Duryodhana.

PRATIKAMI (-MIN).‚ÄîOf the Suta caste; the messenger attending on Duryodhana who goes to Draupadi to inform her that she had been made a slave in the game of dice. Some take it as a common name meaning ‚Äòmessenger,‚Äô som as the proper name of that particular messenger.

PRATIPA.‚Äî A king of the line of Bharata; father of king Santanu.

**PRATISMRITI.‚Äî**A Mantra ; it is by the power of this Mantra that Arjuna wins the favour of God Siva and Indra and gets divine missiles from them.

**PRATIVINDHYA.‚Äî**Son of Yudhisthira and Draupadi,

PRISHATA.‚Äî The father of Drupada, king of the Panchalas; he was the son of king Somaka. From him king Drupada takes the name Parshata and Draupadi, as Parshata’s daughter, is referred to as Parshati.

**PRITHA-KUNTI.‚Äî**Daughter of Sura, the Yadava chief; originally called Pritha, but later called Kunti having been adopted as daughter by a cousin of Sura, king Kuntibhoja of the Bhojas; first wife of Pandu; mother of the first three Pandavas, Yudhishthira, Bhima and Arjuna.

**PUROCHANA.‚Äî**A minister and ally of Duryodhana; Duryodhana entrusts him

with the task of burning the Pandavas in the lac house at Varanavata; instead, the
Pandavas burn him in the same lac house and escape.

RADHA.‚Äî Wife of Adhiratha and fostermother of Karna; through her, Karna gets the name Radheya.

RAJASUYA.‚Äî One of the sacrifices performed by ancient kings; Yudhisthira performs it.

RAMA.‚Äî The incarnation of God Vishnu previous to His incarnation as Krishna; son of Dasaratha of the solar race, hence known as Dasarathi; mentioned here as a great exemplar of righteous rule.

RATI.‚Äî Consort of Madana; goddess of Love.

**RAUDRA ASTRA.‚Äî**Rudra-missile; another divine missile which Karna wants to aim at Arjuna but is not able to.

RUDRAS.‚Äî The eleven Devas of that name.

SAHADEVA.‚Äî Fifth and last Pandava; son of Madri, born by her invokation of the Asvins; famed as a scholar; also referred to as Madreya, etc. (Madri’s son).

**SAIRANDHRI.‚Äî**A lady attendant adept in toilet; the guise in which Draupadi spends her incognito life in Virata’s harem.

SAKTI.‚Äî A pike-like powerful missile; Karna had one such given to him by Indra, which Karna was keeping in store to kill Arjuna but which he had to use against Ghatotkacha.

Yudhishthira aims a Sakti and kills his uncle, Salya.

SAKUNI.‚Äî Son of the king of the Gandharas, Subala, and hence called Saubala; brother of Gandhari and uncle of Duryodhana; Duryodhana’s evil genius; great cheat and adept at dice; is killed by Sahadeva in the great battle.

Also referred to as Gandhara and Gandhararaja (prince of the Gandharas).

SALYA.‚Äî Madra prince (Madraraja, Madradhipa, Madresvara), brother of Madri (second wife of Pandu), uncle of the twins, Nakula and Sahadeva; referred to as uncle to the other Pandavas and to Duryodhana also; a warrior equal to Krishna in valour and in driving the horses; he was proceeding to the Pandavas on the eve of the great war but was cleverly secured by Duryodhana for his side; drives the chariot for Karna and after Karna’s fall, becomes the commander of Duryodhana’s forces for half a day on the eighteenth day of the battle; is killed by Yudhisthira.

**SAMSAPTAKAS.‚Äî**Warriors who swear profusely while fighting; the forces of the king of the Trigartas, his son Susarman and others, who fight for Duryodhana and are destroyed by Arjuna.

SANJAYA.‚Äî The charioteer, minister and messenger of Dhritarashtra; of the Suta caste; hence referred to as Suta, Sutaputra; Gavalgani (son of Gavalgana).

SANTANU.‚Äî Son of king Pratipa; marries Ganga and gives birth to Bhishma; then marries Satyavati, already mother of Vyasa,

and gives birth to Chitrangada whodies early and Vichitravirya who succeeds him on the throne.

SARASVATI.‚Äî A river. The Kamyaka forest is said to be on its banks.

**SATANIKA.‚Äî**Son of Nakula and Draupadi.

SATAYUPA.‚Äî A Rajarshi, a king who had retired and taken to ascetic life; living near Vyasasrama; Dhritarashtra, Gandhari, Kunti, Vidura and Sanjaya, who retire into the forests, stay for some time there and get initiated into ascetic life.

SATVATAS.‚Äî A clan of people who were kinsmen of Krishna; hence is Krishna called Satvata, and Subhadra, Satvati.

**SATYABHAMA.‚Äî**A wife of Krishna.

**SATYAVATI.‚Äî**Daughter of Uparichara Vasu; foster-daughter of the chief of the fishermen; mother of Vyasa as a maiden; later married to Santanu; mother ofChitrangada and Vichitravirya. Referred to also as Daseyi (fisherman’s daughter).

**SAUBHAPATI.‚Äî**King Salva, whom Amba, the eldest daughter of the Kasi king, wants to marry; Saubha is the name of his capital which, it is said, was a huge Vimana which he could move at will.

**SIKHANDIN.‚Äî**Eldest son of Drupada; he was originally a girl and then there was a sex transformation in her; he led a squadron of forces for the Pandavas and was employed to kill Bhishma; for Bhishma was vowed not to fight eunuchs, women or such as had been women once.

** SISUPALA.‚Äî** King of the Chedis; also called Sunitha; an enemy of Krishna. (The Vidarbha princess Rukmini, who wanted to marry Krishna, was about to be given in marriage to Sisupala by her eldest brother, Rukmin, but Krishna carried her away and married her). Sisupala questions Krishna’s greatness in Yudhisthira’s Rajasuya and is slain by Krishna.

**SIVA.‚Äî**God Siva; one of the Hindu Trinity; mentioned as comparison for great prowess; is propitiated by Arjuna; bestows on Arjuna the Pasupata missile. Othernames Sankara, Isana, Rudra, Hara, Vrishabhadhvaja.

SIVA.‚Äî Name of the lac house where Purochana lodges the Pandavas at Varanavata.

SKANDA.‚Äî The boy war-god, born of Siva and Parvati, who led the Devas against the Asuras; also called Pavaki, son of Pavaka (god of fire) who also plays a part in the story of his origin.

**SOMAKAS.‚Äî**The Panchalas; the name is after king Somaka, grandfather of Drupada; allies fighting on the side of the Pandavas in the great battle.

**SRUTAKARMAN.‚Äî**Son of Arjuna and Draupadi.

**SRUTASENA.‚Äî**Son of Sahadeva and Draupadi.

SUBALA.‚Äî The king of the Gandharas; his daughter is Gandhari, the wife of

Dhritarashtra; his son is the villain of the Epic, Sakuni, uncle of Duryodhana.

SUBHADRA.‚Äî Krishna’s sister; one of Arjuna’s wives; mother of Abhimanyu. Also called Satvati, after her race.

**SUDESHNA.‚Äî**Virata’s queen.

SUMITRA.‚Äî The king of the Sauvira people whom Arjuna puts down, as soon as Yudhisthira is appointed as Yuvaraja.

SURA.‚Äî The Yadava chief; father of Vasudeva and grandfather of Krishna; father of Kunti, mother of the first three Pandavas.

**SUTASOMA.‚Äî**Son of Bhima and Draupadi.

SVA.‚Äî The dog in the form of which God Dharma follovs Yudhishthira in his journey towards heaven and tests his Dharma.

**TANTRIPALA.‚Äî**Sahadeva’sname as the cowherd of Virata.

TRIGARTAS.‚Äî The country lying close to the Matsyas; inimical to the Matsyas and friendly to Duryodhana; often laid waste by Kichaka, commander of the Matsya forces.

UPAPLAVYA.‚Äî The city in the Matsyadesa where the Pandavas stay at the end of their one year’s incognito life in the Viratanagara; near the capital; it is from there that peace talks are conducted by the Pandavas.

UTTARA.‚Äî Daughter of king Virata; wife of Abhimanyu, Arjuna’s son; mother of Parikshit.

** VAJRA.‚Äî** Krishna’s grandson; survives the Yadavas; is installed as king by Arjuna at Sakra-(Indra) prastha.

VAJRANABHA.‚Äî This is taken as a descriptive attribute of the discus presented to Krishna by Agni; some take it also as another name of Krishna’s Chakra, Sudarsana.

VALALA.‚Äî The namewhich Bhima as cook assumes in his incognito life atVirata’s court.

VALANA.‚Äî An ally and assistant of Duryodhana who helps the latter to poison Bhima’s food.

VARANAVATA.‚Äî A city lying close to the capital of the Kauravas, Hastinapura; the Pandavas are asked to go there to witness the festival of Siva and an attempt is made to burn them in a lac house there.

VASUDEVA.‚Äî A Yadava; son of Sura; Krishna’s father; Matula (uncle of the first three Pandavas), Sauri (son of Sura).

**VASUS.‚Äî**A group of the Devas, eight in number; Bhishma is an incarnation of a Vasu; in the end, he joins them.

VAYU.‚Äî God Vayu; invoked by Kunti; gives birth to Bhima, the second Pandava.

VEDANGAS.‚Äî The six lores auxiliary to the Vedas: Phonetics, Prosody, Grammar, Etymology, Astronomy, and Ritual codes.

VEDAS.‚Äî The revealed scriptures of the Hindus.

** VICHITRAVIRYA.‚Äî** Second son of Santanu and Satyavati; succeeds his brother Chitrangada on the latter’s death; married by Bhishma to two daughters of the Kasi king; becomes prey to a wasting disease through indulgence in pleasures, and dies childless.

VIDURA.‚Äî Born by Vyasa’s Niyoga to Sudra maid-servant of Ambika; the minister of the house of the Kauravas; a partial incarnation of God Dharma; stands by Dharma at all costs; loved by Krishna and the Pandavas and loves the Pandavas for their Dhar na; renowned for his wisdom; hence called Vidura and referred to as Mahamati; also referred to as Kshatta (born of a Sudra wife).

VIKARNA.‚Äî One of the hundred sons, and the only righteous son, of Dhritarashtra; boldly voices forth his view at the end of the game of dice that Draupadi has not been made a slave.

VIRATA.‚Äî The king of the Matsyas; Matsyaraja, Matsya.

**VIRATADESA.‚Äî**The country where the Pandavas live their incognito life for a year.

**VIRATANAGARA.‚Äî**The capital city of the Virata territory.

**VISVAKARMAN.‚Äî**The architect of the gods in heaven; asked by Indra to rebuild the city of Khandavaprastha for Yudhisthira.

VRISHNIS.‚Äî A race of Krishna’s kinsmen, after whom Krishna gets his name Varshneya.

VYASA.‚Äî The author of the Mahabharata; asage; born to Satyavati and sage Parasara, when the former was a maiden; half-brother of Vichitravirya, son of Satyavati and Santanu; raises issue through Niyoga on Vichitravirya’s wives; thus father of Dhritarashtra, Pandu and Vidura; appears at critical times to help the Pandavas. Other names: Krishna, Dvaipayana (born on an island), Satyavatisuta (son of Satyavati); once referred to as Bharata Pitamaha, (grandfather of the Bharatas).

VYASA ASRAMA.‚Äî The abode of Vyasa in the Himalayas; the penance-grove named Badarikasrama.

YADAVAS.‚Äî A Western Indian race named after the ancestor Yadu; the race of Krishna and Kunti, the mother of the Pandavas.

YAKSHA.‚Äî A semi-divine being; God Dharma, Yudhisthira’s father, takes the form of a Yaksha and as a crane appears in the enchanted lake in the forest and tests Yudhisthira’s Dharma.

YAMUNA.‚Äî A river flowing from the Himalayas and joining the Ganges; the Jumna; Santanu meets Satyavati on its banks.

**YAMUNA ADRIRAJA.‚Äî**That part of the Himalayas where the Jumna has its rise.

YAMAU.‚Äî The twin-sons of Madri, Nakula and Sahadeva.

**YATUDHANAS.‚Äî**Demons; the hundred sons of Dhritarashtra, who were manifestations of demons, get merged into the demons after their death.

YAVANADHIPA.‚Äî King of the Yavana people whom Arjunavanquishes, as soon asYudhisthira is made Yuvaraja.

**YUDHISTHIRA.‚Äî**Eldest son of Pandu; borne by Kunti by invoking God Dharma; the hero of the Epic. Other names: Dharmaraja (the righteous king), Dharmaputra (son of God Dharma), Ajatasatru (one who had no enemy), Ajamidha (scion of Ajamidha, grandfather of Kuru); also referred to as king.

**YUYUDHANA.‚Äî**Son of Satyaka, hence called Satyaki; a Yadava chief; kinsman of Krishna; accomparies Krishna when he goes on the great embassy; fights for the Pandavas.

** YUYUTSU.‚Äî**Son of Dhritarashtra and his Vaisya wife; joins the Pandavas in the great battle; the one surviving member of the line of Dhritarashtra; appointed regent for Parikshit by the Pandavas on their journey to the heavens; referred to also as Vaisyaputra.

First Edn. 3,000 Copies Nov. 1935, G. A. Natesan & Co., Madras.

‚ÄúNo work of the imagination that could be named, always excepting the Iliad, is so rich and so true as the Mahabharata in the portraiture of the human character‚Äìnot in torment and suffering as in Dante, not under overwhelming passions as in Shakespeare‚Äîbut human character in its calm dignity of strength and repose, like those immortal figures in marble which the ancients turned out, and which modern sculptors have vainly sought to reproduce. The old Kuru monarch Dhritarashtra, sightless and feeble, but majestic in his ancient grandeur; the noble grandsire Bhishma, ‚Äúdeath’s subduer‚Äù and unconquerable in war; the doughty Drona, venerable priest and vengeful warrior; and the proud and peerless archer Karna‚Äîhave each a distinct character of his own………….The proud and unyielding Duryodhan, and the fierce and fiery Duhsasan stand out foremost among the wrathful sons of the feeble old Kuru monarch. And Krishna………….unmatched in human wisdom, ever striving for righteousness and peace, he is thorough and unrelenting in war when war has begun. And the women of the Indian Epic possess characters as marked as those of the men. The stately and majestic queen Gandhari, the loving and doting mother Pritha, the proud and scornful Draupadi nursing her wrath till her wrongs are fearfully revenged, and the bright and brilliant and sunny Subhadra,‚Äîthese are distinct images pencilled by the hand of a true master in the realm of creative imagination.‚ÄîR. C. Dutt.

THE INDIAN EPICS
THE RAMAYANA AND THE MAHABHARATA

TWO UNIFORM VOLUMES
Texts in Devanagari and English Translation

The Ramayana. Condensed in Valmiki’s own words. Translated into English by Prof. P. P. S. Sastri, B.A. (Oxon.), M.A. With a Foreword by the Rt. Hon. Dr. V. S. Srinivasa Sastri, P.C., C.H.

The Mahabharata. Condensed in sage Vyasa’s own words by Pandit A. M. Srinivasachari. Translated into English by Dr. V. Raghavan, M.A., Ph.D. With a Foreword by Dr. Sir 8. Radhakrishnan.

In the condensed versions of these two great Epics the thread of the main story is presented clearly together with the best portions of the dialogues and the essence of the discourses, unburdened by the big digressions. The stories are told in the words of the Poets themselves; in the case of theRamayana it is the poet Valmiki that isspeaking, and in the case of the Mahabharata it is the sage Vyasa.

The translation is done in simple and elegant English prose and every attempt is made to preserve the spirit of the original in the English rendering.

It is sincerely hoped that this popular edition of the Great Indian Epics will find its way to thousands of homes in India and elsewhere and will find favour with the students of our schools and colleges.

CONDENSED IN THE POET’S OWN WORDS

The Text in Devanagari and English Translation

PROF. P. P. S. SASTRI, B.A. (OXON). M.A.
FOREWORD BY

THE RT. HON, SRINIVASA SASTRI, P.C., C.H., LL.D.

Mr. Natesan, who published over a quarter of a century ago a popular edition of theBhagavad Gita and also of the Select Works of Sri Sankaracharya withthe text in Devanagari and anEnglishtranslation, has now enriched Indianclassicalliterature with another valuable publication quite unique in character. The story is told by the poet himself; the passages placed before the reader are selected passages from the poem itself. We have the story of the epic in full together with the renowned dialogues, the beautiful character sketches and the many inimitable descriptions.

Ramanand to Ram Tirath

This book includes sketches of Ramanand and Kabir, Nanak and the Sikh Gurus, of Ravi Das the Chamar Saint, of Mira Bai the ascetic queen of Chitor, Vallabhacharya, Tulsidas, Virajanand, Dayanand and Ram Tirath.

Price Re. 1-8. To Subs. of the ‚ÄúI.R‚Äù, Re. 1-4.

Chaitanya to Vivekananda

In this book are presented the sketches of six saints: five Bengali and one Assamese.

HINDU ETHICS
PRINCIPLES OF HINDU RELIGIO-SOCIAL REGENERATION
BY BABU GOVINDA DAS

INTRODUCTION BY BABU BHAGAVAN DAS
AND A FOREWORD

BY DR. GANGANATHA JHA, M.A., D.Litt.

A companion volume to the author’s book on Hinduism. It is critical of current Hindu beliefs and lays down lines along which reform should proceed.
